<div id="review_119686936" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/119686936" />
    <a title="Kathy Davie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4222001-kathy-davie"><img alt="Kathy Davie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1285089902p2/4222001.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/119686936?book_show_action=true">Sep 01, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathy Davie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathy Davie" href="/user/show/4222001-kathy-davie">Kathy Davie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4222001-kathy-davie?shelf=erotica">erotica</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4222001-kathy-davie?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer119686936" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15844619053214318395">First in the Meredith Gentry erotic urban fantasy series revolving around a part-brownie, part-fey, part-human Faerie princess who fled Faerie lest she die. The story takes place in Los Angeles and in Cahokia, Illinois.<br/><br/><b>My Take</b><br/>I want to say there was less depth to this story than in her Anita Blake series, although it's possible that the similarity of her Merry character is simply too much like Anita, and it feels as though Hamilton is cheating, that she can't be bothered to create another strong</span>
  <span id="freeText15844619053214318395" style="display:none">First in the Meredith Gentry erotic urban fantasy series revolving around a part-brownie, part-fey, part-human Faerie princess who fled Faerie lest she die. The story takes place in Los Angeles and in Cahokia, Illinois.<br /><br /><b>My Take</b><br />I want to say there was less depth to this story than in her Anita Blake series, although it's possible that the similarity of her Merry character is simply too much like Anita, and it feels as though Hamilton is cheating, that she can't be bothered to create another strong female character who is her own individual. And yet, Merry <em>is</em> strong. If only Hamilton had left off some of those tell-tale Blake signature moves...	<br /><br />I do enjoy Hamilton’s imagination and the twists into which it takes her. It’s a tale of faeries and goblins, magic and things that go bump in the night. It’s the Seelie and Unseelie with merely a mention of the former. It's the action that never stops as Hamilton takes what we “know” of the fey and twists it round and round: tension, drama, and an exciting combination of humanity and eros.<br /><br />Politics, intrigue, murder, sex, and pain. Yes, be prepared for a descent into BDSM for Merry likes her pain, although <em>A Kiss of Shadows</em> merely dips its toe into the sting and throb of Merry’s preferences. <br /><br /><em>A Kiss of Shadows</em> beautifully sets the series up with its background of the fae and Merry herself along with the cast of characters and how they intertwine. I love how simply Hamilton drops in the underlying plot for the series, how she sets us up, and then ties it into this story while exciting our imaginations for the next, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30240.A_Caress_of_Twilight" target="_blank" title="Opens Laurell K. Hamilton's A Caress of Twilight in Goodreads" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <em>A Caress of Twilight</em>
</a>, 2.<br /><br />It’s a gorgeous example of <em>not</em> using info dumps! <br /><br />Each of the guards chosen by the queen’s ring is unique with his own strengths and weaknesses. Some I like, some intrigue, and others…hmmm, I’m not sure yet…<br /><br />It’s a book that reads so easily that the pages fly by as piece by piece, the parts of Faerie that are dying call to Meredith, respond to her.<br /><br /><b>The Story</b><br />Having fled the Unseelie Court three years ago, Merry has lived with the worry of discovery all that time. If her aunt should ever find her, her death will be the least of Merry’s concerns.<br /><br />But it seems that the power is dying in the Unseelie Court and perhaps, just perhaps, Merry has the power to bring life back.<br /><br /><b>The Characters</b><br /><b>Meredith “Merry Gentry” NicEssus</b>, half-Seelie and half-Unseelie sidhe, is one of the weakest members of the royal sidhe court and hiding in Los Angeles as a private detective. <b>Roane Finn</b> is an skinned Selkie and Merry’s boyfriend. <b>Keelin Nic Brown</b>, a goblin-brownie half-breed, was Merry’s childhood friend. <b>Essus</b> was the Prince of Flame and Flesh, and Merry’s father, the queen’s brother. <b>Gran</b> is half-human, half-brownie; <b>Uar the Cruel</b> of the Seelie Court was her husband because she bore him twins, one of whom was Merry's mother. Now Gran runs a bed-and-breakfast.<br /><br /><b>Jeremy Grey</b>, a trow, is her boss at the Grey Detective Agency, which specializes in supernatural cases, and they have the personnel to back that up. <b>Uther Squarefoot</b>, a jack-in-irons, is a thirteen-foot giant while<b> Ringo</b> is a human who made a deal with the fey. <b>Teresa</b> is the resident psychic. <b>Eileen Galan</b> of James, Browning, and Galan is the lawyer representing Merry.<br /><br /><b>Detective Lucy Tate</b> has worked with the Grey Detective Agency in the past. <b>Detective John Wilkes</b> has a lot to learn. <b>Detective Alvera</b> learns more than he wants. <b>Maury Klein</b> is a civilian sound expert, the best in L.A. And totally oblivious to Merry’s charms. <b>Chris</b> is his diplomatic assistant. <br /><br /><b>Frances Norton</b> is the wife and <b>Naomi Phelps</b> is the mistress of a man who terrifies them both: <b>Alistair Norton</b>. <b>Liam</b>, <b>Donald</b>, and <b>Brendan</b> are his partners in crime.<br /><br />The <b>Queen of Air and Darkness</b> is the queen of the Unseelie Court, and <b>Aunt Andais</b>, a sexual sadist. None of her guard are allowed to have sex with anyone but her. <b>Eamon</b> is the queen’s royal consort. <b>Fflur</b> is a healer fey and a weaver. <b>Ezekial</b> is the queen’s torturer.<br /><br /><b>Prince Cel</b> is her son and makes Hannibal Lecter seem like a dozy grandfather. <b>Siobhan</b> is Cel’s right hand. <b>Rozenwyn</b> is another of his guards, Cel’s second-in-command, and one who challenged Merry to a duel and left her marked by her hand of power. <b>Conri</b> is one of Cel’s friends, and he tries to hurt Merry by challenging Galen. <b>Pasco</b> is Rozenwyn’s twin, and the spy the queen sends to Merry’s bed.<br /><br /><b>Sholto</b> is King of the Sluagh, the leader of the Host, Lord of Shadows, and Lord of That Which Passes Between with the jealous hags---<b>Nerys the Grey</b>, <b>Segna the Gold</b>, and <b>Black Agnes</b>---as his confidantes or lovers. <br /><br /><em>The Ravens are the Queen’s Guards:</em><br /><b>Doyle</b> is the Queen’s Darkness, her right hand; his carrying <b>Mortal Dread</b>, another one of the queen’s private weapons, proves he comes from her. <b>Galen</b> was/is Merry’s childhood friend and love. The fey she would have loved to marry.<b> Barinthus</b> had been worshipped as a sea god, and he’s Old Court Sidhe, a power to be reckoned with. The fearsome <b>Frost</b> who carries <b>Geamhradh Po’g</b> Winter’s Kiss, a great sword, is feeling awkward. <b>Rhys</b> is a death god. <b>Nicca</b> is another spy with butterfly wings.<br /><br /><b>Queen Niceven</b> is of the demi-fey with a hold over Meredith.<br /><br /><b>Kurag</b> is king of the goblins with a taste for Meredith. <b>Kitto</b> is a snake goblin whom Kurag gives over to Merry to seal their alliance.<br /><br />The <b>King of Light and Illusion</b> of the Seelie Court is her uncle. <br /><br /><b>Jenkins</b> is a scumbag of a journalist who’s been tracking Meredith for years, capitalizing on her misfortunes.<br /><br /><b>Bureau of Human Fey Affairs</b>. <b>Griffin</b> was her lover before he cruelly left her. The <b>Black Coach</b> of the wild hunt is sentient and thinks for itself.<br /><br /><b>My Cover</b><br />The cover is symbolic of Aunt Andais’ court: all blood and death with its red background and blackened roses as they curl up and around Merry’s naked legs.<br /><br />The title is our introduction into Merry’s homeland, merely <em>A Kiss of Shadows</em> before we plunge deeper.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15844619053214318395" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2373699793" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2373699793" />
    <a title="Silvia Andrito" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38352861-silvia-andrito"><img alt="Silvia Andrito" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1595864065p2/38352861.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2373699793?book_show_action=true">Apr 26, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Silvia Andrito" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Silvia Andrito" href="/user/show/38352861-silvia-andrito">Silvia Andrito</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2373699793" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12300963933477067269">I’ll start with a little bit of background of my experience with Ms. Hamilton’s writing. About 10 years ago I started reading the Anita Blake series. At first, I liked it a lot but as the series progressed the crimes got gorier, the sex got more meaning-less (she just started having sex with everyone), in some ways it became repetitive. It was very formulaic. She would find one impossible crime that was very gory, she will be the only person who could fix it and then she will have sex with more,</span>
  <span id="freeText12300963933477067269" style="display:none">I’ll start with a little bit of background of my experience with Ms. Hamilton’s writing. About 10 years ago I started reading the Anita Blake series. At first, I liked it a lot but as the series progressed the crimes got gorier, the sex got more meaning-less (she just started having sex with everyone), in some ways it became repetitive. It was very formulaic. She would find one impossible crime that was very gory, she will be the only person who could fix it and then she will have sex with more, and more people. I made it through the first 10 books. But I got fatigued and did not want to read any more of them as they were, like I said, repetitive and, in some ways, just trying to outdo each other in the gory and sex department. Anita Blake went from being a person that did not have sex with just anyone to be the complete opposite; a person that had sex with just about everyone. It started being very confusing as to what relationship she was in (or who she was doing). And why she was doing some of the things that she was doing. Basically, everyone was game for sex. Which was the opposite of how this character started. <br /><br />After 10 years of not reading anything by Ms. Hamilton I decided to pick up her Merry Gentry series. I had not read it in all these years because I felt that I would not like it as much as I did the original Anita (first few books). Also, because the subject was not as interesting to me. I am not the biggest fan of Fae court stories. But while I waited for another book that I am very interested in to come out I decided to pick up A Kiss of Shadows just to keep myself entertained. <br /><br />A lot of reviewers said that it was just bad porn. Others said that it was a great story, even better than Anita Blake. As far as I can tell yes, it’s very porn-like. But that did not bother me as much at the beginning since she made it part of the story. Mary is not human she is Fae, she has different views and how she approaches sex in general is much different than humans. Her having sex with different characters is interpreted from the beginning as her just being different and the author just trying to drive that point home. <br /><br />Where the story started lacking for me was when the actual plot started being developed. I thought that she would be a P.I. in LA and we would get to see that. But that was not the case, that was only the very beginning of the book. When the book starts she has no powers, has no connections in the court, and she is running from her aunt, the queen. But as the book progresses characters are introduced, made to seem important, then promptly become irrelevant to the story right after they almost have sex in one way or another. Which made it seem unnecessary and a waste of the reader’s time. <br /><br />After she gets to the court I thought that things would pick up, but it just becomes assassination attempt after assassination attempt in a way that was not really intriguing or interesting. A lot of the events seem to be glossed over and the story is just not interesting enough to make the reader care about the characters. It becomes all about sex; connections, alliances, anything and everything, the currency is blood or sex. Then she gets forced to have to make a child with one of 27 men, so sex became kind of a chore. This made it repetitive and not interesting.<br /><br />Honestly, I wanted to get into the series. I wanted to like it as much as I once liked Anita Blake back at the very beginning. But from the very beginning it is all just sex and gore. While some of the story is interesting it was not captivating enough for me to want to read the next book. Frankly it was just a little bit too much. The sex was interesting and sexy sometimes, but other times it was just there. As far as the story you are introduced to a main character whose situation changes tremendously from the beginning of the book to the end of the book. The problem I had with this was that it did not reflect growth on the character. It just felt abrupt and forced at times. She went from being a powerless no-one running for her life, to being a very powerful heir to the throne. This is told in the summary at the beginning. I just figured that it would happen more naturally versus wham-bam go from point A to point B in no time. <br /><br />As far as the other characters around her, this is a reverse harem so there are a lot of male characters surrounding her. Some of them are very interesting from the get go like Darkness, and Frost. But they do not really get developed. They just have a sexual encounter with her, and that’s it. I assume that they will be developed further on in the series. The evil characters are interesting enough, the queen is portrayed as crazy and merciless yet protective of her son. Her son, like a spoiled brat that has gone crazy with power. Both of which are cruel sadists. The family history is given very quickly and there is a lot of information which is not easy to process. I found it very confusing and had to reread a couple of times to try and figure out who was who and from which court. It gets confusing as the story is told. I kept thinking that I had it figured out just to realize that I was thinking of it completely wrong. I am sure that everything will be further developed later. I just really would have wished that the background story of the family would have been given enough development from the get go. And that it had not been so confusing.<br /><br />I will not continue reading this series. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12300963933477067269" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_353517166" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/353517166" />
    <a title="Lisa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1512868-lisa"><img alt="Lisa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1269709619p2/1512868.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/353517166?book_show_action=true">Jun 22, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisa" href="/user/show/1512868-lisa">Lisa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1512868-lisa?shelf=kindle-baby">kindle-baby</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1512868-lisa?shelf=2012">2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1512868-lisa?shelf=bollocks">bollocks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1512868-lisa?shelf=irritating-heroines">irritating-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1512868-lisa?shelf=angels-fairies-and-wispy-things">angels-fairies-and-wispy-things</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1512868-lisa?shelf=childhood-reads">childhood-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1512868-lisa?shelf=smut">smut</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1512868-lisa?shelf=wouldnt-touch-him-with-yours">wouldnt-touch-him-with-yours</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer353517166" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13647938451683079774">I thought I'd give Laurell K Hamilton another chance, that my problems with the Anita Blake series might be confined to that series and Anita herself. I was wrong. In this, a different series starring Merry Gentry, the half-human sidhe princess, everything that irritated me most about Anita was front and centre; the feeling that the heroine is an author avatar for Hamtilon to 'live out' her fantasies, pages and pages of descriptions on the most awful outfits imaginable, the heroine standing arou</span>
  <span id="freeText13647938451683079774" style="display:none">I thought I'd give Laurell K Hamilton another chance, that my problems with the Anita Blake series might be confined to that series and Anita herself. I was wrong. In this, a different series starring Merry Gentry, the half-human sidhe princess, everything that irritated me most about Anita was front and centre; the feeling that the heroine is an author avatar for Hamtilon to 'live out' her fantasies, pages and pages of descriptions on the most awful outfits imaginable, the heroine standing around while those around her discuss how beautiful she is, every male she meets lusting after her, and every circumstance dealt with through liberal application of sex, all of which is decidedly unerotic. There's no real effort at characterisation other than Merry being the most beautiful, most fascinating, most wonderful creature to have ever walked the earth - take it as read that every male will want her more than they've ever wanted anyone before, and every woman will see her as a threat. It amuses me to think Hamilton might want to see herself this way too. I'm convinced she's not getting enough.<br /><br />In hiding from her sidhe family, Merry is working at a detective agency. Not for long though, as she's summoned back to the Unseelie Court, goes to see the Queen, and is ordered to have sex with loads of men. And that's it. The initial 'mystery' is solved without Merry really even thinking about it, as she instead rubs herself up against anyone who crosses her path, including those with tentacles.<br /><br />I'm no prude by any stretch of the imagination so my problem with the constant sex was less to do with being squicky about it and more to do with being insanely bored by it all. I find that the most erotic scenes I've read have usually had some sort of build-up and some investment, emotional or otherwise, is always helpful. Sex is used in this book as almost akin to shaking hands, and it strips it of any eroticism it might have otherwise had. <br /><br />There's not much else for me to say other than to try and remind myself not to pick up any more Hamilton in the future, as we really don't get along. In Merry and Anita's worlds, that would mean I was sexually threatened or jealous. Bless.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13647938451683079774" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_122446642" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/122446642" />
    <a title="Angela" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4255477-angela"><img alt="Angela" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1398251387p2/4255477.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/122446642?book_show_action=true">Sep 19, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angela" href="/user/show/4255477-angela">Angela</a>
      </span>

          added it


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6632391-a-kiss-of-shadows">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Angela by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/4625936-wendy">Wendy</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=good-n-cheap">good-n-cheap</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer122446642" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1219380527719633808">7 April 2014: $1.99 on Kindle - Had to share! Bwahahahaha!! Probably because there's a new book (finally) slated to come out this summer! //<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('oun1AI3r1fTA/lqOOZsuM9nvyYgCC2er69docuSgPuewcejiwPsTO54Q2ijJl7XqhZdXKvPsPcEAzJsgYotNPA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('hcfXrp68h1pUtEmCyZV7+k7JqIoRywRDtRZoeiSe/6uXX8pM06xBlQpaySQ5meAjErE2KOAsXileDZsoorWMcA==')})
  }
//]]>

He is a Monère, one of the children of the moon-and what\'s more, so is she.\n\nLong exiled from the moon, the men of the Monère serve-and mate-with imperious Queens who can channel the rays of their far-off homeland. Gryphon believes that Mona Lisa is a Queen- perhaps the first of Mixed Blood ever known. But her introduction to the nighttime court of the Monère, simmering with intrigue, casual lust, and calculated cruelty, is far from smooth. The other Queens are infuriated by her potential powers, and they are all menaced by a group of rogue males who have broken away from the women\'s sway. Even as she battles threats from within and without, Mona Lisa is determined to discover who she is, and to explore the limits of her growing power-and her secret desires.<\/span>\n  <a <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer13841967295717335681">Laurell K. Hamilton is one of the leading writers of paranormal fiction. A #1 New York Times bestselling author, Hamilton writes the popular Anita Blake, Vampire Hunter novels and the Meredith Gentry series. She is also the creator of a bestselling comic book series based on her Anita Blake novels and published by Marvel Comics. Hamilton is a full-time writer and lives in the suburbs of St. Louis </span>
